Objectively speaking her story is great.  Subjectively speaking, I don't like how she was handled in the comics. The 'Fire Siblings' are a textbook example of the two main methods kids use to survive in abusive households.  Zuko's method; being meek and submissive in nature to avoid any threats, perceived or not.  Azula's method; becoming useful to the abuser by emulating their characteristics.  And yet it's portrayed as the wrong choice, rather than what is likely her *only* choice. Let's not kid ourselves with modern ideas. The world of Avatar is inspired by various South Asian and Pacific cultures Pre-Enlightenment, and subsequently the idea of Human Rights, and civility. Azula was either going to be married off at a very young age, or killed by Zuko to solidify his claim to the throne by right of being the only living family member able to sit, as Iroh was in his twilight years, AND willingly abdicated his claim to the crown.  The Heir and The Spare, one is destined to die, the other to rule. A tale as old as the concept of leadership and power.  Also, can we talk about how horrifying a mental asylum in the Dark Ages would be? Shit dude, no wonder she spiraled even further, the staff probably have no clue what they're doing and are just making it up as they go.

The hair band thing is a reference to Japan's Shoguns. They would grow their hair out long and then do it up in a pony tail. If they were dishonored, they'd cut the ponytail off, and have to get it back in blood. (that last part might be wrong, but I'm setting the scene)  Zuko still had his hairband because even in exile, he was still the Crown Prince, so he still had that clout. Iroh was a respected veteran, and so he kept his on... Eventually, when Zuko and Iroh get jumped because the fecking captain of that boat spoke the quiet part aloud, they cut their hair in disgrace. And for the rest of the series, they're doing one of three things: Laying low, fighting Aang, or trying to get it back in blood against Azula or the Fire Lord
